Differences between amounts scheduled by the Debtors and claims by creditors will be investigated and resolved in connection with the claims resolution process. In light of the\nexpected number of creditors, the claims resolution process may take considerable time to complete and will likely continue after our emergence from bankruptcy. Accordingly, the ultimate number and amount of allowed claims is not presently known,\nnor can the ultimate recovery with respect to allowed claims be presently ascertained.  To the best of our\nknowledge, we have notified all of our known current or potential creditors that the Debtors have filed chapter 11 cases. The Schedules and Statements set forth, among other things, the assets and liabilities of each of the Debtors, including\nexecutory contracts to which each of the Debtors is a party, and are subject to the qualifications and assumptions included therein and amendment or modification as our chapter 11 cases proceed. \nThrough the claims resolution process, differences in amounts scheduled by the Debtors and claims filed by creditors will\nbe investigated and resolved, including through the filing of objections with the Bankruptcy Court where appropriate.  Many of the claims identified in the Schedules and Statements are listed as disputed, contingent or unliquidated. In addition, there are differences between the amounts for certain claims listed in the\nSchedules and Statements and the amounts claimed by our creditors. Such differences, as well as other disputes and contingencies will be investigated and resolved as part of our claims resolution process in our chapter 11 cases. Please refer to Note\n11 for additional information about contingent matters and commitments related to certain claims filed in our chapter 11 cases.  Pursuant to the Federal Rules of Bankruptcy Procedure, some creditors who wished to assert prepetition claims against us and whose claims (i)\xc2\xa0were not listed in the Schedules and Statements or\n(ii)\xc2\xa0were listed in the \n \xc2\xa0 52 \n\n\n\n\n\nTable of Contents\n\n \nSchedules and Statements as disputed, contingent, or unliquidated, were required to file a proof of claim with the Bankruptcy Court prior to the bar date set by the court. The bar date for non-governmental creditors was September\xc2\xa01, 2016, and the bar date for governmental creditors was October\xc2\xa026, 2016.  The claims filed against the Debtors to date are voluminous. Further, it is possible that claimants will file amended or modified claims in the future, including modifications or amendments to assign\nvalues to claims originally filed with no designated value. The amended or modified claims may be material. \nWe plan to investigate and evaluate all filed claims in connection with our plan of reorganization. As a part of the\nclaims resolution process, we anticipate working to resolve differences in amounts we listed in our Schedules and Statements and amounts of claims filed by our creditors. We have already identified, for example, claims that we believe should be\ndisallowed by the Bankruptcy Court because they are duplicative, have been later amended or superseded, are without merit, are overstated or for other reasons. We have previously filed, and we will continue to file and prosecute, objections with the\nBankruptcy Court as necessary for claims we believe should be disallowed.  Tax Attributes; Net Operating Loss\nCarryforwards  We have substantial tax net operating loss carryforwards and other tax attributes. Under\nthe U.S. Internal Revenue Code, our ability to use these net operating losses and other tax attributes may be limited if we experience a change of control, as determined under U.S. Internal Revenue Code. Accordingly, we obtained an order from the\nBankruptcy Court that is intended to protect our ability to use our tax attributes by imposing certain notice procedures and transfer restrictions on the trading of the Company\xc2\x92s common stock. \nIn general, the order applies to any person or entity that, directly or indirectly, beneficially owns (or would\nbeneficially own as a result of a proposed transfer) at least 4.5% of the Company\xc2\x92s common stock. Such persons are required to notify us and the Bankruptcy Court before effecting a transaction that might result in us losing the ability to use\nour tax attributes, and we have the right to seek an injunction to prevent the transaction if it might adversely affect our ability to use our tax attributes.  Any purchase, sale or other transfer of our equity securities in violation of the restrictions of the order is null and would be treated as invalid from the outset as an act in violation of a Bankruptcy\nCourt order and would therefore confer no rights on a proposed transferee. Petition Date on excess cash over normal invested capital. \nAbility to Continue as a Going Concern \nThe Consolidated Financial Statements included in this Annual Report on Form 10-K\nhave been prepared on a going concern basis of accounting, which contemplates continuity of operations, realization of assets, and satisfaction of liabilities and commitments in the normal course of business. The Consolidated Financial Statements do\nnot reflect any adjustments that might result from the outcome of our chapter 11 proceedings. We have significant indebtedness, all of which we have reclassified to liabilities subject to compromise at December\xc2\xa031, 2016. Our level of\nindebtedness has adversely impacted and is continuing to adversely impact our financial condition. As a result of our financial condition, the defaults under our debt agreements, and the risks and uncertainties surrounding our chapter 11\nproceedings, substantial doubt exists that we will be able to continue as a going concern.  Critical Accounting Policies \nThe discussion and analysis of the Company\xc2\x92s financial condition and results of operations is based upon consolidated\nfinancial statements, which have been prepared in accordance with U.S.\xc2\xa0GAAP. In addition, application of GAAP requires the use of estimates, judgments and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities as of the date of\nthe financial statements as well as the revenues and expenses reported during the period. Changes in these estimates related to judgments and assumptions will occur as a result of future events, and, accordingly, actual results could differ from\namounts estimated. Set forth below is a discussion of the critical accounting policies used in the preparation of our financial statements which we believe involve the most complex or subjective decisions or assessments. \nOil and Gas Reserves.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0The reserve estimates presented herein were made in accordance\nwith oil and gas reserve estimation and disclosure authoritative accounting guidance according to Financial Accounting Standards Board (\xc2\x93FASB\xc2\x94) Accounting Standards Codification (\xc2\x93ASC\xc2\x94) Topic 932, Extractive Activities \xc2\x97 Oil\nand Gas (\xc2\x93FASB ASC 932\xc2\x94) as updated in order to align the reserve calculation and disclosure requirements with those in SEC Release No.\xc2\xa033-8995. \n \xc2\xa0 54 \n\n\n\n\n\nTable of Contents\n\n The Company utilizes reliable technology such as seismic data and\ninterpretation, wireline formation tests, geophysical logs and core data to assess its resources. However, none of these technologies have contributed to a material addition to the proved reserves in this report. \nEstimates of proved crude oil and natural gas reserves significantly affect the Company\xc2\x92s depreciation, depletion\nand amortization (\xc2\x93DD&A\xc2\x94) expense. For example, if estimates of proved reserves decline, the Company\xc2\x92s DD&A rate will increase, resulting in a decrease in net income. A decline in estimates of proved reserves may result from a\nnumber of factors including lower prices, evaluation of additional operating history, mechanical problems on our wells and catastrophic events. Lower prices also make it uneconomical to drill wells or produce from fields with high operating costs.\n The Company\xc2\x92s proved reserves are a function of many assumptions, all of which could deviate materially\nfrom actual results. As a result, the estimates of proved reserves could vary over time, and could vary from actual results.  Full Cost Method of Accounting.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0The Company uses the full cost method of accounting for exploration and development activities as defined by the Securities and\nExchange Commission (\xc2\x93SEC\xc2\x94) Release No.\xc2\xa033-8995, Modernization of Oil and Gas Reporting Requirements (\xc2\x93SEC Release No.\xc2\xa033-8995\xc2\x94) and\nFinancial Accounting Standards Board (\xc2\x93FASB\xc2\x94) Accounting Standards Codification (\xc2\x93ASC\xc2\x94) Topic 932, Extractive Additives \xc2\x97 Oil and Gas (\xc2\x93FASB ASC 932\xc2\x94). Under this method of accounting, the costs of unsuccessful, as\nwell as successful, exploration and development activities are capitalized as oil and gas properties. This includes any internal costs that are directly related to exploration and development activities but does not include any costs related to\nproduction, general corporate overhead or similar activities. The carrying amount of oil and natural gas properties also includes estimated asset retirement costs recorded on the fair value of the asset retirement obligation when incurred. Gain or\nloss or other disposition of oil and natural gas properties is not recognized, unless the gain or loss would significantly alter the relationship between capitalized costs and proved reserves of oil and natural gas attributable to a country.\n The sum of net capitalized costs and estimated future development costs of oil and natural gas properties are\namortized using the units-of-production method based on the Company\xc2\x92s proved reserves. Oil and natural gas reserves and production are converted into equivalent\nunits based on relative energy content. Asset retirement costs are included in the base costs for calculating depletion.  Under the full cost method, costs of unevaluated properties and major development projects expected to require significant future costs may be excluded from capitalized costs being amortized. The Company\nexcludes significant costs until proved reserves are found or until it is determined that the costs are impaired. The Company reviews its unproved leasehold costs quarterly or when management determines that events or circumstances indicate that the\nrecorded carrying value of the unevaluated properties may not be recoverable. The fair values of unproved properties are evaluated utilizing a discounted net cash flows model based on management\xc2\x92s assumptions of future oil and gas production,\ncommodity prices, operating and development costs; as well as appropriate discount rates. The estimated prices used in the cash flow analysis are determined by management based on forward price curves for the related commodities, adjusted for\naverage historical location and quality differentials. Estimates of cash flows related to probable and possible reserves are reduced by additional risk weighting factors. The amount of any impairment is transferred to the capitalized costs being\namortized.  Write-down of Oil and Gas\nProperties.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0Companies that use the full cost method of accounting for oil and natural gas exploration and development activities are required to perform a ceiling test calculation each quarter. The\nfull cost ceiling test is an impairment test prescribed by SEC Regulation\xc2\xa0S-X Rule\xc2\xa04-10. The ceiling test is performed quarterly, on a country-by-country basis, utilizing the average of prices in effect on the first day of the month for the preceding twelve month period in accordance with SEC Release No.\xc2\xa033-8995. The ceiling limits such pooled costs to the aggregate of the present value of future net revenues attributable to proved crude oil and natural gas reserves discounted at 10%, plus the lower of cost\nor market value of unproved properties, less any \n \xc2\xa0 55 \n\n\n\n\n\nTable of Contents\n\n \nassociated tax effects. If such capitalized costs exceed the ceiling, the Company will record a write-down to the extent of such excess as a non-cash\ncharge to earnings. Any such write-down will reduce earnings in the period of occurrence and results in a lower depletion, depreciation and amortization (\xc2\x93DD&A\xc2\x94) rate in future periods. A write-down may not be reversed in future\nperiods even though higher oil and natural gas prices may subsequently increase the ceiling.  During 2015, the\nCompany recorded a $3.1\xc2\xa0billion non-cash write-down of the carrying value of the Company\xc2\x92s proved oil and gas properties as a result of ceiling test limitations, which is reflected with ceiling test\nand other impairments in the accompanying Consolidated Statements of Operations. The ceiling test was calculated based upon the average of quoted market prices in effect on the first day of the month for the preceding twelve month period at\nDecember\xc2\xa031, 2015 for Henry Hub natural gas and West Texas Intermediate oil, adjusted for market differentials. The Company did not have any write-downs related to the full cost ceiling limitation in 2016 or 2014. \nDeferred Financing Costs.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0During the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2016, a non-cash charge to write-off all of the unamortized debt issuance costs related to the unsecured Credit Agreement, unsecured Senior Notes (as defined below) issued by Ultra\nResources, Inc., the unsecured 2018 Senior Notes (as defined below) issued by the Company and the unsecured 2024 Senior Notes (as defined below) issued by the Company is included in Reorganization items, net in the accompanying Consolidated\nStatements of Operations as these debt instruments are expected to be impacted by the pendency of the Company\xc2\x92s chapter 11 cases. At December\xc2\xa031, 2015, other current assets includes costs associated with the issuance of our revolving\ncredit facility while costs associated with the issuance of our Senior Notes, 2018 Notes and 2024 Notes are presented as a direct deduction from the carrying amount of the related debt liability. \nAsset Retirement Obligation.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0The Company\xc2\x92s asset retirement obligations\n(\xc2\x93ARO\xc2\x94) consist primarily of estimated costs of dismantlement, removal, site reclamation and similar activities associated with its oil and natural gas properties. FASB ASC Topic 410, Asset Retirement and Environmental Obligations\n(\xc2\x93FASB ASC 410\xc2\x94) requires that the discounted fair value of a liability for an ARO be recognized in the period in which it is incurred with the associated asset retirement cost capitalized as part of the carrying cost of the oil and\nnatural gas asset. The recognition of an ARO requires that management make numerous estimates, assumptions and judgments regarding such factors as the existence of a legal obligation for an ARO, estimated probabilities, amounts and timing of\nsettlements; the credit-adjusted, risk-free rate to be used; inflation rates, and future advances in technology. In periods subsequent to initial measurement of the ARO, the Company must recognize period-to-period changes in the liability resulting from the passage of time and revisions to either the timing or the amount of the original estimate of undiscounted cash flows. Increases in the ARO\nliability due to passage of time impact net income as accretion expense. The related capitalized costs, including revisions thereto, are charged to expense through DD&A. \nEntitlements Method of Accounting for Oil and Natural Gas Sales.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0The Company\ngenerally sells oil and natural gas under both long-term and short-term agreements at prevailing market prices and under multi-year contracts that provide for a fixed price of oil and natural gas. The Company recognizes revenues when the oil and\nnatural gas is delivered, which occurs when the customer has taken title and has assumed the risks and rewards of ownership, prices are fixed or determinable and collectability is reasonably assured. The Company accounts for oil and natural gas\nsales using the \xc2\x93entitlements method.\xc2\x94 Under the entitlements method, revenue is recorded based upon the Company\xc2\x92s ownership share of volumes sold, regardless of whether it has taken its ownership share of such volumes. \nMake-up provisions and ultimate settlements of volume imbalances are generally\ngoverned by agreements between the Company and its partners with respect to specific properties or, in the absence of such agreements, through negotiation. The value of volumes over- or under-produced can change based on changes in commodity prices.\nThe Company prefers the entitlements method of accounting for oil and natural gas sales because it allows \n \xc2\xa0 56 \n\n\n\n\n\nTable of Contents\n\n \nfor recognition of revenue based on its actual share of jointly owned production, results in better matching of revenue with related operating expenses, and provides balance sheet recognition of\nthe estimated value of product imbalances.  Valuation of Deferred Tax\nAssets.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0The Company uses the asset and liability method of accounting for income taxes. Under this method, future income tax assets and liabilities are determined based on differences between the financial statement\ncarrying values and their respective income tax basis (temporary differences).  To assess the realization of\ndeferred tax assets, management considers whether it is more likely than not that some portion or all of the deferred tax assets will not be realized. The ultimate realization of deferred tax assets is dependent upon the generation of future taxable\nincome during the periods in which those temporary differences become deductible. Management considers the scheduled reversal of deferred tax liabilities, projected future taxable income and tax planning strategies in making this assessment.\n The Company has recorded a valuation allowance against certain deferred tax assets of $1.3\xc2\xa0billion as of\nDecember\xc2\xa031, 2016. Some or all of this valuation allowance may be reversed in future periods against future income.  Derivative Instruments and Hedging Activities.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0The Company follows FASB ASC Topic 815, Derivatives and Hedging (\xc2\x93FASB ASC 815\xc2\x94). The Company records the fair\nvalue of its commodity derivatives as an asset or liability on the Consolidated Balance Sheets, and records the changes in the fair value of its commodity derivatives in the Consolidated Statements of Operations as an unrealized gain or loss on\ncommodity derivatives.  Fair Value Measurements.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0The Company follows FASB\nASC Topic 820, Fair Value Measurements and Disclosures (\xc2\x93FASB ASC 820\xc2\x94). Under FASB ASC 820, fair value is defined as the price that would be received to sell an asset or paid to transfer a liability in an orderly transaction between\nmarket participants at measurement date and establishes a three level hierarchy for measuring fair value. The valuation assumptions the Company has used to measure the fair value of its commodity derivatives were observable inputs based on market\ndata obtained from independent sources and are considered Level\xc2\xa02 inputs (quoted prices for similar assets, liabilities (adjusted) and market-corroborated inputs). See Note\xc2\xa08 for additional information. \nLegal, Environmental and Other Contingencies.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0A provision for legal, environmental\nand other contingencies is charged to expense when the loss is probable and the cost can be reasonably estimated. Determining when expenses should be recorded for these contingencies and the appropriate amounts for accrual is a complex estimation\nprocess that includes the subjective judgment of management. In many cases, management\xc2\x92s judgment is based on interpretation of laws and regulations, which can be interpreted differently by regulators and/or courts of law. The Company\xc2\x92s\nmanagement closely monitors known and potential legal, environmental and other contingencies and periodically determines when the Company should record losses for these items based on information available to the Company. \nShare-Based Payment Arrangements.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0The Company follows FASB ASC Topic 718,\nCompensation \xc2\x97 Stock Compensation (\xc2\x93FASB ASC 718\xc2\x94) which requires the measurement and recognition of compensation expense for all share-based payment awards made to employees and directors, including employee stock options, based on\nestimated fair values. Share-based compensation expense recognized under FASB ASC 718 for the years ended December\xc2\xa031, 2016, 2015 and 2014 was $5.6\xc2\xa0million, $4.1\xc2\xa0million and $5.5\xc2\xa0million, respectively. See Note\xc2\xa06 for\nadditional information.  Conversion of Barrels of Oil to Mcfe of\nGas.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0The Company converts barrels of oil and other liquid hydrocarbons to Mcfe at a ratio of one barrel of oil or liquids to six Mcfe. This conversion ratio, which is typically used in the oil and gas\nindustry, represents the approximate energy equivalent of a barrel of oil or other liquids to an Mcf of natural gas. The sales price of one barrel of oil or liquids has been much higher than the sales price of six Mcf of natural gas over the last\nseveral years, so a six to one conversion ratio does not represent the economic equivalency of six Mcf of natural gas to a barrel of oil or other liquids. \n \xc2\xa0 57 \n\n\n\n\n\nTable of Contents\n\n Recent accounting pronouncements. \nRestricted Cash.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0In November 2016, the FASB issued ASU\n2016-18,\xc2\xa0Statement of Cash Flows (Topic 230): Restricted Cash (\xc2\x93ASU No.\xc2\xa02016-18\xc2\x94). The guidance requires that an explanation is included in\nthe cash flow statement of the change in the total of (1)\xc2\xa0cash, (2) cash equivalents, and (3)\xc2\xa0restricted cash or restricted cash equivalents. The ASU also clarifies that transfers between cash, cash equivalents and restricted cash or\nrestricted cash equivalents should not be reported as cash flow activities and requires the nature of the restrictions on cash, cash equivalents, and restricted cash or restricted cash equivalents to be disclosed. For public companies, the standard\nwill take effect for fiscal years, and interim periods within those fiscal years, beginning after December\xc2\xa015, 2017 with earlier application permitted. The Company does not expect the adoption of this ASU to have a material impact on its\nconsolidated financial statements.  Statement of Cash Flows.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0In August 2016, the\nFASB issued ASU 2016-15,\xc2\xa0Statement of Cash Flows (Topic 230) (\xc2\x93ASU No.\xc2\xa02016-15\xc2\x94). The guidance requires that debt prepayment or debt\nextinguishment costs, including third-party costs, premiums paid, and other fees paid to lenders, be classified as cash outflows for financing activities. For public companies, the standard will take effect for fiscal years, and interim periods\nwithin those fiscal years, beginning after December\xc2\xa015, 2017 with earlier application permitted. The Company does not expect the adoption of this ASU to have a material impact on its consolidated financial statements. \nShare-Based Payment.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0In March 2016, the FASB issued Accounting Standards Update\n(\xc2\x93ASU\xc2\x94) 2016-09, Compensation-Stock Compensation (Topic 718): Improvements to Employee Share-Based Payment Accounting (\xc2\x93ASU No.\xc2\xa02016-09\xc2\x94)\nto simplify some of the provisions in stock compensation accounting. The update simplifies the accounting for a stock payment\xc2\x92s tax consequences and amends how excess tax benefits and a business\xc2\x92s payments to cover the tax bills for the\nshares\xc2\x92 recipients should be classified. The amendments allow companies to estimate the number of stock awards expected to vest and revises the withholding requirements for classifying stock awards as equity. For public companies, the standard\nwill take effect for fiscal years, and interim periods within those fiscal years, beginning after December\xc2\xa015, 2016 with earlier application permitted. The Company is still evaluating the impact of ASU\nNo.\xc2\xa02016-09 on its financial position and results of operations. \nLeases.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0In February 2016, the FASB issued\nASU2016-02, Leases (\xc2\x93ASU No.\xc2\xa02016-02\xc2\x94). The guidance requires that lessees will be required to recognize assets and liabilities on\nthe balance sheet for the rights and obligations created by all leases with terms of more than 12 months. The ASU will also require disclosures designed to give financial statement users information on the amount, timing, and uncertainty of cash\nflows arising from leases. These disclosures include qualitative and quantitative information. For public companies, the standard will take effect for fiscal years, and interim periods within those fiscal years, beginning after December\xc2\xa015,\n2018 with earlier application permitted. The Company is still evaluating the impact of ASU No.\xc2\xa02016-02 on its financial position and results of operations. \nInventory.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0In July 2015, the FASB issued ASU\n2015-11, Inventory (Topic 330): Simplifying the Measurement of Inventory (\xc2\x93ASU No.\xc2\xa02015-11\xc2\x94). Public companies will have to apply the amendments\nfor reporting periods that start after December\xc2\xa015, 2016, including interim periods within those fiscal years. This ASU requires an entity to measure inventory at the lower of cost and net realizable value. Net realizable value is the estimated\nselling prices in the ordinary course of business, less reasonably predictable costs of completion, disposal, and transportation. The company does not expect the adoption of ASU No.\xc2\xa02015-11 to have a\nmaterial impact on its consolidated financial statements.  Debt Issuance\nCosts.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0In April 2015, the FASB issued ASU 2015-03, Interest \xc2\x97 Imputation of Interest (Subtopic 835-30) \xc2\x97 Simplifying the\nPresentation of Debt Issuance Costs. In August 2015, the FASB issued ASU 2015-15, Interest \xc2\x97 Imputation of Interest (Subtopic 835-30) \xc2\x97 Presentation and\nSubsequent Measurement of Debt Issuance Costs Associated with Line-of-Credit Arrangements. These ASUs require capitalized debt issuance costs, except for those\nrelated to revolving credit facilities, to be presented in the balance sheet as a direct deduction from the carrying amount of the related debt liability, rather than as an asset. The Company \n\n \xc2\xa0 58 \n\n\n\n\n\nTable of Contents\n\n \nadopted these ASUs on January\xc2\xa01, 2016, using a retrospective approach. The adoption resulted in a reclassification that reduced current assets and current maturities of long-term debt by\n$19.4\xc2\xa0million on the Company\xc2\x92s Consolidated Balance Sheet at December\xc2\xa031, 2015. A non-cash charge to write-off all of the unamortized debt issuance costs\nis included in Reorganization items, net at December\xc2\xa031, 2016 as the related debt instruments are expected to be impacted by the pendency of the Company\xc2\x92s chapter 11 cases. \nRevenue Recognition.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0In May 2014, the FASB issued ASU\n2014-09, Revenue from Contracts with Customers (Topic 606) and in 2016, the FASB issued ASU 2016-08, Revenue from Contracts with Customers (Topic 606): Principal versus\nAgent Considerations (Reporting Revenue Gross versus Net), and ASU 2016-10, Revenues from Contracts with Customers (Topic 606): Identifying Performance Obligations and Licensing, which supersede the revenue\nrecognition requirements in Topic 605, Revenue Recognition, and industry-specific guidance in Subtopic 932-605, Extractive Activities-Oil and Gas-Revenue Recognition. The new standard requires an entity to recognize revenue when it transfers promised goods or services to customers in an amount that reflects the consideration the entity expects to be\nentitled to in exchange for those goods or services.  We are currently evaluating the provisions of ASU 2014-09 and assessing the impact, if any, it may have on our financial position and results of operations. As part of our assessment work to date, we have dedicated resources to the implementation, completed\ntraining of the new ASU\xc2\x92s revenue recognition model, and begun contract review and documentation. The primary impacts to the Company of adopting ASU 2014-09 relate to principal versus agent considerations\nand the use of the entitlements method for oil and natural gas sales, both of which are continuing to be evaluated by the Company.  The Company is required to adopt the new standards in the first quarter of 2018 using one of two application methods: retrospectively to each prior reporting period presented (full retrospective method),\nor retrospectively with the cumulative effect of initially applying the guidance recognized at the date of initial application (the cumulative catch-up transition method). The Company is currently evaluating\nthe available adoption methods.  Going Concern.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0In August 2014, the FASB issued\nASU No.\xc2\xa02014-15, Disclosure of Uncertainties about an Entity\xc2\x92s Ability to Continue as a Going Concern (\xc2\x93ASU No.\xc2\xa02014-15\xc2\x94) that requires\nmanagement to evaluate whether there are conditions and events that raise substantial doubt about the Company\xc2\x92s ability to continue as a going concern within one year after the financial statements are issued on both an interim and annual\nbasis. Management is required to provide certain footnote disclosures if it concludes that substantial doubt exists or when its plans alleviate substantial doubt about the Company\xc2\x92s ability to continue as a going concern. ASU No.\xc2\xa02014-15 becomes effective for annual periods ending after December\xc2\xa015, 2016 and for interim reporting periods thereafter. The adoption of this ASU did not have a material impact on the Company\xc2\x92s\nConsolidated Financial Statements. \n \xc2\xa0 59 \n\n\n\n\n\nTable of Contents\n\n Results of Operations \xc2\x97 Year \nProduction.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0During the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2016, production decreased on a gas\nequivalent basis to 281.7\xc2\xa0Bcfe from 290.1\xc2\xa0Bcfe for the same period in 2015. The decrease is primarily attributable to decreased capital investment during the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2016. \nCommodity prices \xc2\x97 natural gas.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0Realized natural gas prices decreased to $2.31 per Mcf\nduring the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2016 as compared to $2.59 per Mcf during 2015. The Company did not have any open \n \xc2\xa0 60 \n\n\n\n\n\nTable of Contents\n\n \nderivative contracts for natural gas production during 2016. During the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015, the Company\xc2\x92s average price for natural gas was $3.14 per Mcf, including realized\ngains and losses on commodity derivatives.  Commodity prices \xc2\x97 oil.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0During\nthe year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2016, the average price realization for the Company\xc2\x92s oil was $38.24 per barrel compared with $40.31 per barrel during 2015. The Company did not have any open derivative contracts for oil production during 2016\nor 2015.  Revenues.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0The decrease in average oil and natural gas prices and\ndecreased total production resulted in revenues decreasing to $721.1\xc2\xa0million for the for the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2016 as compared to $839.1\xc2\xa0million in 2015.  Operating Costs and Expenses:  Lease Operating\nExpense.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0Lease operating expenses (\xc2\x93LOE\xc2\x94) decreased to $89.1\xc2\xa0million for the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2016 compared to $106.9\xc2\xa0million during the same period in 2015 largely related to lower costs\ndue to improved efficiencies. On a unit of production basis, LOE costs decreased to $0.32 per Mcfe at December\xc2\xa031, 2016 compared to $0.37 per Mcfe at December\xc2\xa031, 2015. \nLiquids Gathering System Operating Lease Expense.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0During December 2012, the Company\nsold a system of liquids gathering pipelines and central gathering facilities (the \xc2\x93Pinedale LGS\xc2\x94) and certain associated real property rights in the Pinedale Anticline in Wyoming. The Company entered into a long-term, triple net lease\nagreement with the buyer relating to the use of the Pinedale LGS (the \xc2\x93Pinedale Lease Agreement\xc2\x94). The Pinedale Lease Agreement provides for an initial term of 15 years, and annual rent for the initial term under the Pinedale Lease\nAgreement is $20.0\xc2\xa0million (as adjusted annually for changes based on the consumer price index) and may increase if certain volume thresholds are exceeded. The lease is classified as an operating lease. For the year ended December\xc2\xa031,\n2016, the Company recognized operating lease expense associated with the Pinedale Lease Agreement of $20.7\xc2\xa0million, or $0.07 per Mcfe compared with $20.6\xc2\xa0million, or $0.07 per Mcfe in 2015. \nProduction Taxes.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0During the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2016, production taxes were\n$69.7\xc2\xa0million compared to $72.8\xc2\xa0million during the same period in 2015, or $0.25 per Mcfe in 2016, compared to $0.25 per Mcfe in 2015. Production taxes are primarily calculated based on a percentage of revenue from production in Wyoming\nand Utah after certain deductions and were 9.7% of revenues for the year ended 2016 and 8.7% for the same period in 2015. The decrease in production taxes is primarily attributable to decreased oil and natural gas prices during the year\nDecember\xc2\xa031, 2016 as compared to the same period in 2015.  Gathering\nFees.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0Gathering fees decreased slightly to $86.8\xc2\xa0million for the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2016 compared to $87.9\xc2\xa0million during the same period in 2015. On a per unit basis, gathering fees increased slightly\nto $0.31 per Mcfe for the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2016 as compared to $0.30 per Mcfe for the period ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015.  Transportation Charges.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0Transportation charges decreased to $20.0\xc2\xa0million for the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2016 as compared to $83.8\xc2\xa0million for the same period\nin 2015 primarily as a result of the termination of the Rockies Express contract during the second quarter of 2016. See Note 13 and Note 11 for further discussion of the Rockies Express contract. \nDepletion, Depreciation and Amortization.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0DD&A expenses decreased to\n$125.1\xc2\xa0million during the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2016 from $401.2\xc2\xa0million for the same period in 2015, attributable to a decreased depletion rate on a unit of production basis as a result of the ceiling test impairment during the\nfourth quarter of 2015. On a unit of production basis, DD&A decreased to $0.44 per Mcfe at December\xc2\xa031, 2016 from $1.38 per Mcfe at December\xc2\xa031, 2015. \n \xc2\xa0 61 \n\n\n\n\n\nTable of Contents\n\n Ceiling Test Write-Down.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0The Company recorded\na $3.1\xc2\xa0billion non-cash write-down of the carrying value of its proved oil and natural gas properties for the period ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015 as a result of ceiling test limitations, which is\nreflected as ceiling test and other impairments in the accompanying Consolidated Statements of Operations. The ceiling test was calculated based upon the average of quoted market prices in effect on the first day of the month for the preceding\ntwelve month period at December\xc2\xa031, 2015 for Henry Hub natural gas and West Texas Intermediate oil, adjusted for market differentials. The write-down reduced earnings in the period and will result in lower a DD&A rate in future periods. The\nCompany did not have any write-downs related to the full cost ceiling limitation during the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2016.  General and Administrative Expenses.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0General and administrative expenses increased to $9.2\xc2\xa0million for the period ended December\xc2\xa031, 2016 compared to\n$7.4\xc2\xa0million for the same period in 2015. The increase in general and administrative expenses is primarily attributable to reversal of certain incentive compensation expense during the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015. On a per unit basis,\ngeneral and administrative expenses remained flat at $0.03 per Mcfe for the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2016 and 2015. \nOther Income and Expenses:  Interest Expense.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0Interest expense decreased to $66.6\xc2\xa0million during the period ended December\xc2\xa031, 2016 compared to $171.9\xc2\xa0million during the same period in\n2015. No interest has been recognized subsequent to the petition date of April\xc2\xa029, 2016 (See Note 5). \nLitigation Expense\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0During the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015, the Company recognized\nlitigation expenses of $4.4\xc2\xa0million related to the resolution of litigation matters.  Restructuring\nExpenses.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0During the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2016, the Company incurred $7.2\xc2\xa0million in costs and fees in connection with its efforts to restructure its debt prior to filing the chapter 11 petitions. \nContract Settlement.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0Contract settlement of $131.1\xc2\xa0million for the year ended\nDecember\xc2\xa031, 2016 relates to the contract settlement reached with REX.  Deferred Gain on Sale of\nLiquids Gathering System.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0During the years ended December\xc2\xa031, 2016 and 2015, the Company recognized $10.6\xc2\xa0million in deferred gain on sale of the liquids gathering system relating to the sale of a system of\npipelines and central gathering facilities and certain associated real property rights in the Pinedale Anticline in Wyoming during December 2012.  Commodity Derivatives:  Gain on Commodity\nDerivatives.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0The Company does not currently have any open commodity derivative contracts. During the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015, the Company recognized a gain of $42.6\xc2\xa0million related to commodity derivatives.\nOf this total, the Company recognized $146.8\xc2\xa0million related to realized gain during the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015. The realized gain or loss on commodity derivatives relates to actual amounts received or paid under the\nCompany\xc2\x92s derivative contracts. This gain or loss on commodity derivatives also includes a $104.2\xc2\xa0million unrealized loss on commodity derivatives at December\xc2\xa031, 2015. The unrealized gain or loss on commodity derivatives represents\nthe change in the fair value of these derivative instruments over the remaining term of the contract. Income from Continuing Operations:\n Pretax Income.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0The Company recognized income before income taxes of\n$55.5\xc2\xa0million for the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2016 compared with a loss of $3.2\xc2\xa0billion for the same period in 2015. The increase in earnings is primarily related to the non-cash ceiling test\nimpairment incurred during 2015 and decreased DD&A, reduced interest expense and reduced transportation charges during the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2016; and partially offset by costs associated with the reorganization and decreased revenues\nas a result of lower oil and natural gas prices for the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2016 as compared to the same period in 2015. Some or all of this\nvaluation allowance may be reversed in future periods against future income. The increase in earnings is primarily related to the non-cash ceiling test impairment incurred during 2015 and decreased DD&A, reduced interest expense and reduced transportation\ncharges during the \nProduction.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0During the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015, production increased on a gas\nequivalent basis to 290.1\xc2\xa0Bcfe from 249.0\xc2\xa0Bcfe for the same period in 2014. The increase is primarily attributable to the SWEPI Transaction in September 2014 and our drilling program, offset by expected production declines. Additionally,\non an Mcfe basis, oil production decreased from 8.2% of total production during the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2014 to 7.3% of total production during the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015, primarily as a result of our decision to discontinue\ndrilling in the Uinta Basin in 2015. \n \xc2\xa0 64 \n\n\n\n\n\nTable of Contents\n\n Commodity prices \xc2\x97 natural gas.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0Realized\nnatural gas prices, including realized gains and losses on commodity derivatives, decreased to $3.14 per Mcf during the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015 as compared to $4.03 per Mcf during 2014. During the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015, the\nCompany\xc2\x92s average price for natural gas was $2.59 per Mcf, excluding realized gains and losses on commodity derivatives, as compared to $4.24 per Mcf for the same period in 2014. \nCommodity prices \xc2\x97 oil.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0During the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015, the average\nprice realization for the Company\xc2\x92s oil was $40.31 per barrel compared with $76.47 per barrel during 2014. The Company did not have any open derivative contracts for oil production during 2015. During 2014, the average price realization for the\nCompany\xc2\x92s oil was $76.32, including realized gains and losses on commodity derivatives. \nRevenues.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0The decrease in average oil and natural gas prices, excluding the gains and\nlosses on commodity derivatives, offset by increased production from the properties acquired in the SWEPI Transaction and our drilling program resulted in revenues decreasing to $839.1\xc2\xa0million for the for the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015\nas compared to $1.2\xc2\xa0billion in 2014.  Operating Costs and Expenses: \nLease Operating Expense.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0Lease operating expenses (\xc2\x93LOE\xc2\x94) increased to\n$106.9\xc2\xa0million for the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015 compared to $96.5\xc2\xa0million during the same period in 2014 largely related to increased production associated with the SWEPI Transaction and our drilling program. On a unit of\nproduction basis, LOE costs decreased to $0.37 per Mcfe at December\xc2\xa031, 2015 compared to $0.39 per Mcfe at December\xc2\xa031, 2014.  Liquids Gathering System Operating Lease Expense.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0During December 2012, the Company sold a system of liquids gathering pipelines and central gathering facilities (the\n\xc2\x93Pinedale LGS\xc2\x94) and certain associated real property rights in the Pinedale Anticline in Wyoming. The Company entered into a long-term, triple net lease agreement with the buyer relating to the use of the Pinedale LGS (the \xc2\x93Pinedale\nLease Agreement\xc2\x94). The Pinedale Lease Agreement provides for an initial term of 15 years, and annual rent for the initial term under the Pinedale Lease Agreement is $20.0\xc2\xa0million (as adjusted annually for changes based on the consumer\nprice index) and may increase if certain volume thresholds are exceeded. The lease is classified as an operating lease. For the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015, the Company recognized operating lease expense associated with the Pinedale Lease\nAgreement of $20.6\xc2\xa0million, or $0.07 per Mcfe compared with $20.3\xc2\xa0million, or $0.08 per Mcfe in 2014. \nProduction Taxes.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0During the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015, production taxes were\n$72.8\xc2\xa0million compared to $103.9\xc2\xa0million during the same period in 2014, or $0.25 per Mcfe, compared to $0.42 per Mcfe. Production taxes are primarily calculated based on a percentage of revenue from production in Wyoming and Utah after\ncertain deductions and were 8.7% of revenues for the year ended 2015 and 8.4% for the same period in 2014. The decrease in per unit taxes is primarily attributable to decreased natural gas prices, excluding the effects of commodity derivatives,\nduring the year December\xc2\xa031, 2015 as compared to the same period in 2014.  Gathering\nFees.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0Gathering fees increased to $87.9\xc2\xa0million for the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015 compared to $59.9\xc2\xa0million during the same period in 2014 largely related to production increases in Wyoming. On a per unit\nbasis, gathering fees increased to $0.30 per Mcfe for the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015 as compared to $0.24 per Mcfe for the period ended December\xc2\xa031, 2014 primarily due to higher gathering rates in Wyoming compared to Pennsylvania.\n Transportation Charges.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0The Company incurred firm transportation charges\ntotaling $83.8\xc2\xa0million for the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015 as compared to $77.8\xc2\xa0million for the same period in 2014 in association with REX transportation charges. Transportation charges increased due to a refund received during the\nsecond quarter of 2014 for over collection of tariffs related to Fuel, Loss and Unaccounted-for-Gas applicable to transport on REX\xc2\x92s system. On a per unit basis,\ntransportation charges decreased to $0.29 per Mcfe (on total company volumes) for the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015 as compared to $0.31 per Mcfe for the same period in 2014 primarily as a result of increased production volumes. \n \xc2\xa0 65 \n\n\n\n\n\nTable of Contents\n\n Depletion, Depreciation and\nAmortization.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0DD&A expenses increased to $401.2\xc2\xa0million during the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015 from $293.0\xc2\xa0million for the same period in 2014, attributable to a higher depletion rate and increased\nproduction. On a unit of production basis, DD&A increased to $1.38 per Mcfe at December\xc2\xa031, 2015 from $1.18 per Mcfe at December\xc2\xa031, 2014 primarily related to decreased reserves as a result of not including PUD reserves in total proved\nreserve estimates at December\xc2\xa031, 2015 due to uncertainty regarding our ability to continue as a going concern and the availability of capital that would be required to develop the PUD reserves. \nCeiling Test Write-Down.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0The Company recorded a $3.1\xc2\xa0billion non-cash write-down of the carrying value of its proved oil and natural gas properties for the period ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015 as a result of ceiling test limitations, which is reflected as ceiling test and\nother impairments in the accompanying Consolidated Statements of Operations. The ceiling test was calculated based upon the average of quoted market prices in effect on the first day of the month for the preceding twelve month period at\nDecember\xc2\xa031, 2015 for Henry Hub natural gas and West Texas Intermediate oil, adjusted for market differentials. The write-down reduced earnings in the period and will result in lower a DD&A rate in future periods. The Company did not have\nany write-downs related to the full cost ceiling limitation during the prior year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2014. \nGeneral and Administrative Expenses.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0General and administrative expenses decreased to\n$7.4\xc2\xa0million for the period ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015 compared to $19.1\xc2\xa0million for the same period in 2014. The decrease in general and administrative expenses is primarily attributable to decreased incentive compensation expense and\npersonnel and overhead charges allocated to the increased wells as a result of the SWEPI Transaction. On a per unit basis, general and administrative expenses decreased to $0.03 per Mcfe for the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015 as compared to $0.08\nper Mcfe for the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2014 as a result of decreased costs and increased production.  Other\nIncome and Expenses:  Interest Expense.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0Interest expense increased to\n$171.9\xc2\xa0million during the period ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015 compared to $126.2\xc2\xa0million during the same period in 2014 primarily as a result of higher average borrowings outstanding during the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015 and\ndecreased amounts of capitalized interest for the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015. For the years ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015 and 2014, the Company capitalized $13.1\xc2\xa0million and $20.4\xc2\xa0million, respectively, in interest associated with\nunevaluated oil and gas properties that were excluded from amortization and actively being evaluated as well as work in process relating to gathering systems that are not currently in service. \nLitigation Expense\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0During the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015, the Company recognized\nlitigation expenses of $4.4\xc2\xa0million related to the resolution of litigation matters. Of this total, the Company recognized $146.8\xc2\xa0million related to realized gain on commodity derivatives as compared to $47.7\xc2\xa0million related to realized loss during the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2014. The unrealized gain or loss on commodity derivatives represents the change in the fair value of these derivative instruments\nover the remaining term of the contract.  Income from Continuing Operations: \nPretax Income.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0The Company recognized a loss before income taxes of $3.2\xc2\xa0billion for\nthe year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015 compared with income of $537.0\xc2\xa0million for the same period in 2014. The decrease in earnings is primarily related to the non-cash ceiling test impairment and\ndecreased revenues as a result of lower oil and natural gas prices partially offset by increased production for the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015 as compared to the same period in 2014. \nIncome Taxes.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0The Company has recorded a valuation allowance against substantially all of\nits net deferred tax asset balance as of December\xc2\xa031, 2015. Some or all of this valuation allowance may be reversed in future periods against future income. The income tax benefit recognized for the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015 was\n$4.4\xc2\xa0million compared with an income tax benefit of $5.8\xc2\xa0million for the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2014.  Net Income.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0For the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015, the Company recognized a net loss of $3.2\xc2\xa0billion or -$20.94 per diluted\nshare as compared with net income of $542.9\xc2\xa0million or $3.51 per diluted share for the same period in 2014. The decrease in earnings is primarily related to the non-cash ceiling test impairment and\ndecreased revenues as a result of lower oil and natural gas prices partially offset by increased production for the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2015 as compared to the same period in 2014.  LIQUIDITY AND CAPITAL RESOURCES  Liquidity Before Filing Under\nChapter 11 of the United States Bankruptcy Code  We have historically funded our operations primarily\nthrough cash flows from operating activities, borrowings under the Credit Agreement, proceeds from the issuance of debt and proceeds from asset sales. However, future cash flows are subject to a number of variables, and are highly dependent on the\nprices we receive for oil and natural gas. Oil and natural gas prices declined severely during fiscal year 2015 and declined even further during the first quarter of 2016. The Henry Hub natural gas spot price dropped below $1.65 per MMBtu in March\n2016 for the first time in 17 years. Although natural gas prices have improved in recent months, there is still significant volatility in commodity prices and these prices are still lower than the industry has experienced in recent years. These\nlower commodity prices have negatively impacted revenues, earnings and cash flows, and sustained low oil and natural gas prices will have a material and adverse effect on our liquidity position. \nLiquidity After Filing Under Chapter 11 of the United States Bankruptcy Code \nAs described in Note 1, the filing of the chapter 11 petitions constituted an event of default with respect to our\nexisting debt obligations. However, subject to certain exceptions under the Bankruptcy Code, the filing of the chapter 11 petitions automatically enjoined, or stayed, the continuation of any judicial or administrative proceedings or other actions\nagainst the Debtors or their property to recover, collect or secure a claim arising prior to the filing of the chapter 11 petitions. Thus, for example, most creditor actions to obtain possession of property from the Debtors, or to create, perfect or\nenforce any lien against the Debtors\xc2\x92 property, or to collect on monies owed or otherwise exercise rights or remedies with respect to a pre-petition claim are enjoined unless and until the Bankruptcy\nCourt lifts the automatic stay.  The Bankruptcy Court has approved payment of certain prepetition obligations,\nincluding payments for employee wages, salaries and certain other benefits, customer programs, taxes, utilities, insurance, surety bond premiums as well as payments to possessory lien vendors. Despite the liquidity provided by our existing cash on\n\n \xc2\xa0 67 \n\n\n\n\n\nTable of Contents\n\n \nhand, our ability to maintain normal credit terms with our suppliers may become impaired. We may be required to pay cash in advance to certain vendors and may experience restrictions on the\navailability of trade credit, which would further reduce our liquidity. If liquidity problems persist, our suppliers could refuse to provide key products and services in the future. In addition, due to the public perception of our financial\ncondition and results of operations, in particular with regard to our potential failure to meet our debt obligations, some vendors could be reluctant to enter into long-term agreements with us. \nAlthough we have lowered our capital budget as compared to 2015, our business remains capital intensive. In addition to\nthe cash requirements necessary to fund ongoing operations, we have incurred significant professional fees and other costs in connection with our chapter 11 proceedings and expect that we will continue to incur significant professional fees and\ncosts throughout our chapter 11 proceedings. The Company believes it has sufficient liquidity, including approximately $401.5\xc2\xa0million of cash on hand as of December\xc2\xa031, 2016 and funds generated from ongoing operations, to fund anticipated\ncash requirements through the chapter 11 proceedings for operating and capital expenditures and for working capital purposes and excluding principal and interest payments on our outstanding debt. \nThe Company does not intend to seek\ndebtor-in-possession (\xc2\x93DIP\xc2\x94) financing at this time. However, given the current level of volatility in the market and the unpredictability of certain costs\nthat could potentially arise in our operations, our liquidity needs could be significantly higher than we currently anticipate. There are no assurances that our current liquidity is sufficient to allow us to satisfy our obligations related to the\nchapter 11 cases, proceed with the confirmation of a chapter 11 plan of reorganization and emerge from bankruptcy. We can provide no assurance that we will be able to secure additional interim financing sufficient to meet our liquidity needs or, if\nsufficient funds are available, offered to us on acceptable terms.  Our ability to maintain adequate\nliquidity through the reorganization process and beyond depends on successful operation of our business, and appropriate management of operating expenses and capital spending. Our anticipated liquidity needs are highly sensitive to changes in each\nof these and other factors.  Going Concern.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0The Consolidated Financial\nStatements included in this Annual Report on Form 10-K have been prepared on a going concern basis of accounting, which contemplates continuity of operations, realization of assets, and satisfaction of\nliabilities and commitments in the normal course of business. The Consolidated Financial Statements do not reflect any adjustments that might result from the outcome of our chapter 11 proceedings. We have significant indebtedness, all of which we\nhave reclassified to liabilities subject to compromise at December\xc2\xa031, 2016. Our level of indebtedness has adversely impacted and is continuing to adversely impact our financial condition. As a result of our financial condition, the defaults\nunder our debt agreements, and the risks and uncertainties surrounding our chapter 11 proceedings, substantial doubt exists that we will be able to continue as a going concern. \nInvestors should review the disclosures and other information, including the risk factors included in Item\xc2\xa01A.\n Capital Expenditures.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0For the year ended December\xc2\xa031, 2016, total\ncapital expenditures were $269.6\xc2\xa0million. During this period, the Company participated in 110 gross (78.4 net) wells in Wyoming that were drilled to total depth and cased. The Company also completed 13 drilled but uncompleted wells in Utah\nduring 2016. No wells were drilled in Utah or Pennsylvania during 2016.  2017 Capital Investment\nPlan.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0For 2017, our capital expenditures are expected to be approximately $500.0\xc2\xa0million. We expect to fund these capital expenditures through cash flows from operations and cash on hand. We expect to allocate\nnearly all of the budget to development activities in our Pinedale field. (\xc2\x93Ultra Resources\xc2\x94), a wholly\nowned subsidiary of the Company, is a party to the Credit Agreement. Ultra Resources\xc2\x92 obligations under the Credit Agreement are guaranteed by the Company and UP Energy Corporation, a wholly owned subsidiary of the Company. \nUltra Resources\xc2\x92 filing of the chapter 11 petitions described in Note 1 constituted an event of default that\naccelerated its obligations under the Credit Agreement. Other events of default are also present with respect to the Credit Agreement, including a failure to make interest payments and, as described below, a failure to deliver annual audited\nconsolidated financial statements without a going concern qualification, a failure to meet the minimum PV-9 ratio covenant and a failure to comply with the consolidated leverage covenant in the Credit\nAgreement at the end of the first quarter of 2016. The Credit Agreement provides that upon the acceleration of Ultra Resources\xc2\x92 obligations under the Credit Agreement, the outstanding balance of loans extended under the Credit Agreement comes\ndue, unpaid interest accrued as of the time of the acceleration comes due, and any fees or other obligations of the borrower come due. Under the Bankruptcy Code, the creditors under the Credit Agreement are stayed from taking any action against\nUltra Resources or any of the other Debtors as a result of the default.  Prior to April\xc2\xa029, 2016, loans\nunder the Credit Agreement bore interest, at the borrower\xc2\x92s option, based on (A)\xc2\xa0a rate per annum equal to the prime rate or the weighted average fed funds rate on overnight transactions during the preceding business day plus a margin\nbased on a grid of the borrower\xc2\x92s consolidated leverage ratio, or (B)\xc2\xa0a base Eurodollar rate, substantially equal to the LIBOR rate, plus a margin based on a grid of the borrower\xc2\x92s consolidated leverage ratio. \nThe Credit Agreement requires us to deliver annual audited, consolidated financial statements for the Company without a\n\xc2\x93going concern\xc2\x94 or like qualification or explanation. On March\xc2\xa015, 2016, we delivered an audit report with respect to the financial statements in our 2015 Annual Report on Form 10-K that\nincluded an explanatory paragraph expressing uncertainty as to our ability to continue as a \xc2\x93going concern.\xc2\x94  The Credit Agreement contains a consolidated leverage covenant, pursuant to which Ultra Resources is required to maintain a maximum ratio of its total funded consolidated debt to its trailing four fiscal\nquarters\xc2\x92 EBITDAX of 3.5 to 1.0. Based on Ultra Resources\xc2\x92 EBITDAX for the trailing four fiscal quarters ended March\xc2\xa031, 2016, we were not in compliance with this consolidated leverage covenant at March\xc2\xa031, 2016 (the ratio was\n4.6 times at March\xc2\xa031, 2016).  The Credit Agreement contains a\nPV-9 covenant, pursuant to which Ultra Resources is required to maintain a minimum ratio of the discounted net present value of its oil and gas properties to its total funded consolidated debt of 1.5 times. We\nwere required to report whether we were in compliance with this covenant on April\xc2\xa01, 2016. Based on the PV-9 of its oil and gas properties at December\xc2\xa031, 2015, Ultra Resources failed to comply with\nthe PV-9 ratio covenant under the Credit Agreement (the ratio was 0.9 times at December\xc2\xa031, 2015). This new agreement will provide the Company with\nthe opportunity to transport a portion of its natural gas production away from its properties in Wyoming to capture improved basis differentials available at sales points along the Rockies Express Pipeline, if any. Operating lease.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0During December 2012, the Company sold its system of\npipelines and central gathering facilities (the \xc2\x93Pinedale LGS\xc2\x94) and certain associated real property rights in the Pinedale Anticline in Wyoming and entered into a long-term, triple net lease agreement (the \xc2\x93Pinedale Operating Lease\nAgreement\xc2\x94) relating to the use of the Pinedale LGS. The Pinedale Operating Lease Agreement provides for an initial term of 15 years and potential successive renewal terms of 5 years or 75% of the then remaining useful life of the Pinedale LGS\nat the sole discretion of the Company. Annual rent for the initial term under the Pinedale Operating Lease Agreement is $20.0\xc2\xa0million (as adjusted annually for changes based on the consumer price index, which is 1.05% at January\xc2\xa01, 2017)\nand may increase if certain volume thresholds are exceeded. The lease is classified as an operating lease.  On\nNovember\xc2\xa011, 2016, the Company reached an agreement with the owner of the Pinedale LGS whereby the owner agreed to withdraw its damages claims in exchange for the Company\xc2\x92s subsidiary assuming the Pinedale Operating Lease Agreement with no\ncost to cure.  All of the Company\xc2\x92s lease obligations are related to leases that are classified as\noperating leases.\xc2\xa0These leases contain certain provisions that could result in accelerated lease payments.\xc2\xa0The Company has considered the effect of these provisions on minimum lease payments in its lease classification analysis and has\ndetermined that the default provisions do not impact classification of any the Company\xc2\x92s operating leases. \nOffice space lease.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0The Company maintains office space in Colorado, Texas, Wyoming and Utah\nwith total remaining commitments for office leases of $6.6\xc2\xa0million at December\xc2\xa031, 2016. \n \xc2\xa0 73 \n\n\n\n\n\nTable of Contents\n\n Item\xc2\xa07A. Quantitative and Qualitative Disclosures About Market\nRisk  Objectives and Strategy:\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0The Company\xc2\x92s major market\nrisk exposure is in the pricing applicable to its natural gas and oil production. Realized pricing is currently driven primarily by the prevailing price for the Company\xc2\x92s Wyoming natural gas production. Historically, prices received for natural\ngas production have been volatile and unpredictable. Pricing volatility is expected to continue. As a result of its hedging activities, the Company may realize prices that are less than or greater than the spot prices that it would have received\notherwise.  The Company relies on various types of derivative instruments to manage its exposure to commodity\nprice risk and to provide a level of certainty in the Company\xc2\x92s forward cash flows supporting the Company\xc2\x92s capital investment program.  The Company\xc2\x92s hedging policy limits the amounts of resources hedged to not more than 50% of its forecast production without Board approval. \nFair Value of Commodity Derivatives:\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0FASB ASC 815 requires that all derivatives be\nrecognized on the balance sheet as either an asset or liability and be measured at fair value. Changes in the derivative\xc2\x92s fair value are recognized currently in earnings unless specific hedge accounting criteria are met. The Company does not\napply hedge accounting to any of its derivative instruments.  Derivative contracts that do not qualify for\nhedge accounting treatment are recorded as derivative assets and liabilities at fair value on the balance sheet and the associated unrealized gains and losses are recorded as current expense or income in the income statement. Unrealized gains or\nlosses on commodity derivatives represent the non-cash change in the fair value of these derivative instruments and do not impact operating cash flows on the cash flow statement. \nCommodity Derivative Contracts:\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0At December\xc2\xa031, 2016, the Company had no open\ncommodity derivative contracts to manage price risk on a portion of its production.
